<a name = "spiderman2002may13"></a>
<a href =
"icons/spiderman2002may13-1.jpg"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
><img src = "icons/spiderman2002may13-1.jpg"
width = 100
align = "right" border = 0></a>
<a href =
"icons/spiderman2002may13-2.jpg"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
><img src = "icons/spiderman2002may13-2.jpg"
width = 100
align = "right" border = 0></a>
<a href =
"http://www.lecb.ncifcrf.gov/~toms/leftpolicy.html"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
><img src = "icons/permission.requested.gif" align = "right" border = 0
alt = "permission requested for image"></a>
<li>
In
<a href =
"http://www.apple.com/trailers/columbia/spiderman/"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>the trailer</a>
for the new
<a href =
"http://www.spiderman.sonypictures.com/"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>Spider-man movie</a>,
Spider-man is taking a picture.
Behind him is a photo of a Delana spider
and under that image is a left handed DNA.
The next scene is in a lab is where another <i>different</i>
image of a left-handed DNA is shown.
Clearly Spider-man got his powers from a left handed DNA spider!
The species seems to be
<i>Delena cancerides</i>, which are mentioned in
<a href =
"http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov:80/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&db=PubMed&list_uids=8095195&dopt=Abstract"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>Korszniak and Story (1993)</a>
and
<a href =
"http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov:80/entrez/query.fcgi?cmd=Retrieve&db=PubMed&list_uids=7749579&dopt=Abstract"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>Korszniak and Story (1995)</a>.
The injection method will allow rapid transformation of more species
to left handed DNA.  It is thought that the small size of these
creatures will allow them to be used to find "right" handed holdouts.
<img src="icons/binoc.gif" alt = "binoculars" width = 15 width = 15> First reported on 2002 May 13,
<img src="icons/new.gif" alt = "new"> as of 2002 May 13
<font size = 3 color = #ff00ff>
(Thanks to
Shirley Chan,
chanshir@cshl.edu
for pointing this one out!)
</font>
<br clear = all>

<a name = "cell2002may13"></a>
<!--
<a href =
"http://www.cell.com/"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
><img src = "icons/cell2002may13.gif"
align = "right" border = 0></a>
-->
<a href =
"http://www.lecb.ncifcrf.gov/~toms/leftpolicy.html"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
><img src = "icons/permission.denied.gif" align = "right" border = 0
alt = "permission denied for image"></a>
<li>
A spectacular genetic
control system was
recently discovered by
<a href =
"http://www.cell.com/cgi/content/full/109/3/383/?highlight=109&highlight=383"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>Kim <i>et al</i></a>
(<a href =
"http://www.cell.com/"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>Cell</a>, Vol 109, 383-396, May 2002, Figure 6B)
in which OxyR protein monomers bind to <strong>both</strong>
left and right handed DNA!
   Dr. Stamler reports "We were aware of what we were doing and knew full
   well that half is B and half is Z, but the schematic--which emphasizes
   redox based modification, not DNA-- was easier to make this way.  This is
   why it is a schematic ...  Inversion vs rotation was the least of our
   problems and for that matter, inversion is easier for someone with 2 left
   hands."
<img src="icons/binoc.gif" alt = "binoculars" width = 15> First reported on 2002 May 13,
<img src="icons/new.gif" alt = "new"> as of 2002 May 13
<br clear = all>

<li>
Steve Garavelli reports:
<blockquote>
OK, so I'm checking out
<a href =
"http://www.kartoo.com"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>http://www.kartoo.com</a>
[warning: this url can blow your browser! - TDS]
(a very neat web visualization site mentioned in Science) and I try
"Tom Schneider" expecting to see you stuck in a morass of IT,
and there turns up
<a href =
"http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk</a>
(a furniture company on this side of the pond),
and one of the things listed on
<a href =
"http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk/products.html"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk/products.html</a>
is their "DNA Shelving",
and of course its a left-handed spiral!
</blockquote>
What elegant and lovely furniture, but
of course I will have to
disavow all relationship to cousin Schneider!
The actual images can be found directly in the directory
<a href =
"http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk/tsimages/"
target = "lefthandedDNA"
>http://www.tomschneiderdesigns.co.uk/tsimages/</a>,
in particular the image shown here.

| Thanks for your message. While we are embarassed by our mistake, and would
| willingly be pilloried by your web site, I regret that we cannot give you
| permission to reproduce the image from The Scientist cover of June 24 on
| your web site. We licensed the image (at considerable cost) from a
| commercial image database -- images.com -- for one time use on our cover.

| advise you to remove it.
| 
| Incidentally, your invocation of the "fair use" provision of the Copyright
| Act is inappropriate. Fair use allows a restricted amount of copying for
| personal use. What you are doing is republishing, for all the world to see.
| There is no fair use provision covering publishing.
|

>images.com</a>
sells many cool DNA images (search under each category):
<ul>
<li> Stock illustration Source:
17 images,
8 of which are left handed DNA.
<li> Spots on the Spot:

12 images,
8 of which are left handed DNA.

1 images,
0 of which are left handed DNA.

<P>
<IMG SRC="icons/colorbar.gif">
</p>

<p>
For your first visit to the
<a href = "http://www.lecb.ncifcrf.gov/~toms/LeftHanded.DNA.html">Left Handed
Hall of Fame</a>
 page I suggest that you follow the story
over <a href = Leftwhole.html>all of the years</a>.
After that you can look at each year individually
from the table below.
Note:  just because a year has gone by does not mean
we haven't found more examples for that year!
</p>

<IMG SRC="icons/animouse.gif" ALIGN = "LEFT"></a>
<h1>1997 and 1998 were bumper crop years<br>
and 1999 beat them more than 2 fold.
2000 was a record year, thanks to help from
friends around the world
(60 of the 97 cases, 63%!).
2001 will exceed even that record!
</h1>
<br clear = all>
